             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FF00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             2–3 Children
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #35B0E3; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             1–2 Children
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3555E3; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             0–1 Children
            </div>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </table>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the developing world, birth control increases
      <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">
       economic growth
      </a>
      due to there being fewer dependent children and thus more women participating in the
      <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">
       workforce
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22784535_19-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-pmid22784535-19">
        [19]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Women's earnings, assets,
      <a href="/wiki/Body_mass_index" title="Body mass index">
       body mass index
      </a>
      , and their children's schooling and body mass index all improve with greater access to birth control.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22784535_19-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-pmid22784535-19">
        [19]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">
       Family planning
      </a>
      via the use of modern birth control is one of the most
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cost-effective" title="Cost-effective">
       cost-effective
      </a>
      health interventions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tsui2010_115-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Tsui2010-115">
        [115]
       </a>
      </sup>
      For every dollar spent, the United Nations estimates that two to six dollars are saved.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22784540_16-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-pmid22784540-16">
        [16]
       </a>
      </sup>
      These cost savings are related to preventing unplanned pregnancies and decreasing the spread of sexually transmitted illnesses.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tsui2010_115-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Tsui2010-115">
        [115]
       </a>
      </sup>
      While all methods are beneficial financially, the use of copper IUDs resulted in the greatest savings.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tsui2010_115-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Tsui2010-115">
        [115]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The total medical cost for a pregnancy, delivery and care of a newborn in the United States is on average $21,000 for a vaginal delivery and $31,000 for a
      <a href="/wiki/Caesarean_section" title="Caesarean section">
       Caesarean section
      </a>
      as of 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT2013_116-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT2013-116">
        [116]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In most other countries the cost is less than half.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT2013_116-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT2013-116">
        [116]
       </a>
      </sup>
      For a child born in 2011, an average US family will spend $235,000 over 17 years to raise them.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDAChildExpense_117-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-USDAChildExpense-117">
        [117]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Prevalence">
       Prevalence
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Prevalence">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Prevalence_of_birth_control" title="Prevalence of birth control">
       Prevalence of birth control
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SOWM2010_modern_contraception.svg">
        <img alt="prevalence of modern birth control map" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="940" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/SOWM2010_modern_contraception.svg/220px-SOWM2010_modern_contraception.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/SOWM2010_modern_contraception.svg/330px-SOWM2010_modern_contraception.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/SOWM2010_modern_contraception.svg/440px-SOWM2010_modern_contraception.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SOWM2010_modern_contraception.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Percentage of women using modern birth control as of 2010
        <div>
         <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
          <tr>
           <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             6%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #550000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             12%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #aa0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             18%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             24%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff5500; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             30%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #dddd00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             36%
            </div>
           </td>
           <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #55aa00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             42%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00ff00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             48%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00aa55; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             54%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0055aa; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             60%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             66%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #7700ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             72%
            </div>
           </td>
           <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #aa00ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             78%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff00ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             84%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff77ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             86%
            </div>
            <div class="legend">
             <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b9b9b9; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
             </span>
             No data
            </div>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </table>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Globally, as of 2009, approximately 60% of those who are married and able to have children use birth control.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Darroch2013_118-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Darroch2013-118">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
      How frequently different methods are used varies widely between countries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Darroch2013_118-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Darroch2013-118">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The most common method in the developed world is condoms and oral contraceptives, while in Africa it is oral contraceptives and in Latin America and Asia it is sterilization.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Darroch2013_118-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Darroch2013-118">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the developing world overall, 35% of birth control is via female sterilization, 30% is via IUDs, 12% is via oral contraceptives, 11% is via condoms, and 4% is via male sterilization.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Darroch2013_118-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Darroch2013-118">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      While less used in the developed countries than the developing world, the number of women using IUDs as of 2007 was more than 180 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Darney2010_60-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Darney2010-60">
        [60]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Avoiding sex when fertile is used by about 3.6% of women of childbearing age, with usage as high as 20% in areas of South America.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dar2010p315_119-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dar2010p315-119">
        [119]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 2005, 12% of couples are using a male form of birth control (either condoms or a vasectomy) with higher rates in the developed world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naz2009_120-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Naz2009-120">
        [120]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Usage of male forms of birth control has decreased between 1985 and 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Darroch2013_118-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Darroch2013-118">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Contraceptive use among women in
      <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">
       Sub-Saharan Africa
      </a>
      has risen from about 5% in 1991 to about 30% in 2006.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        [121]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2012, 57% of women of childbearing age want to avoid pregnancy (867 of 1520 million).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dar2013_122-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dar2013-122">
        [122]
       </a>
      </sup>
      About 222 million women however were not able to access birth control, 53 million of whom were in sub-Saharan Africa and 97 million of whom were in Asia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dar2013_122-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dar2013-122">
        [122]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This results in 54 million unplanned pregnancies and nearly 80,000 maternal deaths a year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Darroch2013_118-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-Darroch2013-118">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Part of the reason that many women are without birth control is that many countries limit access due to religious or political reasons,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hopkins2010_2-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hopkins2010-2">
        [2]
       </a>
      </sup>
      while another contributor is
      <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">
       poverty
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rasch2011_123-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rasch2011-123">
        [123]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Due to restrictive
      <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">
       abortion
      </a>
      laws in Sub-Saharan Africa, many women turn to unlicensed abortion providers for
      <a href="/wiki/Unintended_pregnancy" title="Unintended pregnancy">
       unintended pregnancy
      </a>
      , resulting in about 2–4% obtaining
      <a href="/wiki/Unsafe_abortion" title="Unsafe abortion">
       unsafe abortions
      </a>
      each year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rasch2011_123-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rasch2011-123">
        [123]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_birth_control" title="History of birth control">
       History of birth control
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">
       Early history
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Early history">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:181px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Silphium.jpg">
        <img alt="ancient coin depicting silphium" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="164" data-file-width="179" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1c/Silphium.jpg" width="179"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Silphium.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Ancient silver coin from
        <a href="/wiki/Cyrene,_Libya" title="Cyrene, Libya">
         Cyrene
        </a>
        depicting a stalk of
        <a href="/wiki/Silphium" title="Silphium">
         silphium
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Egyptian
      <a href="/wiki/Ebers_Papyrus" title="Ebers Papyrus">
       Ebers Papyrus
      </a>
      from 1550 BCE and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kahun_Papyrus" title="Kahun Papyrus">
       Kahun Papyrus
      </a>
      from 1850 BCE have within them some of the earliest documented descriptions of birth control: the use of honey,
      <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">
       acacia
      </a>
      leaves and lint to be placed in the vagina to block sperm.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History2010_124-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-History2010-124">
        [124]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipsey2005_125-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lipsey2005-125">
        [125]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is believed that in
      <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">
       Ancient Greece
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Silphium" title="Silphium">
       silphium
      </a>
      was used as birth control which, due to its effectiveness and thus desirability, was harvested into extinction.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        [126]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In medieval Europe, any effort to halt pregnancy was deemed immoral by the
      <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
       Catholic Church
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History2010_124-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-History2010-124">
        [124]
       </a>
      </sup>
      although it is believed that women of the time still used a number of birth control measures, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Coitus_interruptus" title="Coitus interruptus">
       coitus interruptus
      </a>
      and inserting lily root and rue into the vagina.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        [127]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Women in the Middle Ages were also encouraged to tie weasel testicles around their thighs during sex to prevent pregnancy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_128-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-:0-128">
        [128]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The oldest condoms discovered to date were recovered in the ruins of
      <a href="/wiki/Dudley_Castle" title="Dudley Castle">
       Dudley Castle
      </a>
      in England, and are dated back to 1640.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_128-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-:0-128">
        [128]
       </a>
      </sup>
      They were made of animal gut, and were most likely used to prevent the spread of sexually transmitted diseases during the
      <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">
       English Civil War
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_128-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-:0-128">
        [128]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Casanova" title="Casanova">
       Casanova
      </a>
      , living in 18th century
      <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
       Italy
      </a>
      , described the use of a lambskin covering to prevent pregnancy; however, condoms only became widely available in the 20th century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History2010_124-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-History2010-124">
        [124]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_control_movement">
       Birth control movement
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Birth control movement">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VictorianPostcard.jpg">
        <img alt="a cartoon of a woman being chased by a stork with a baby" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="258" data-file-width="408" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/VictorianPostcard.jpg/220px-VictorianPostcard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/VictorianPostcard.jpg/330px-VictorianPostcard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bc/VictorianPostcard.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VictorianPostcard.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        "And the villain still pursues her", a satirical
        <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">
         Victorian era
        </a>
        postcard
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The birth control movement developed during the 19th and early 20th centuries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
       <a href="#cite_note-129">
        [129]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Malthusian_League" title="Malthusian League">
       Malthusian League
      </a>
      , based on the ideas of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Malthus" title="Thomas Malthus">
       Thomas Malthus
      </a>
      , was established in 1877 in the United Kingdom to educate the public about the importance of
      <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">
       family planning
      </a>
      and to advocate for getting rid of penalties for promoting birth control.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        [130]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was founded during the "Knowlton trial" of
      <a href="/wiki/Annie_Besant" title="Annie Besant">
       Annie Besant
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bradlaugh" title="Charles Bradlaugh">
       Charles Bradlaugh
      </a>
      , who were prosecuted for publishing on various methods of birth control.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        [131]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the United States,
      <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Sanger" title="Margaret Sanger">
       Margaret Sanger
      </a>
      and Otto Bobsein popularized the phrase "birth control" in 1914.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilk2004_132-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Wilk2004-132">
        [132]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Galvin_133-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Galvin-133">
        [133]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sanger was mainly active in the United States but had gained an international reputation by the 1930s. At the time, under the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comstock_Law" title="Comstock Law">
       Comstock Law
      </a>
      , distribution of birth control information was illegal. She jumped bail in 1914 after her arrest for distributing birth control information and left the United States for the United Kingdom to return in 1915.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        [134]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sanger established a short-lived birth-control clinic based in the Brownville section of
      <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">
       Brooklyn
      </a>
      , New York
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
       <a href="#cite_note-135">
        [135]
       </a>
      </sup>
      in 1916, which was shut down after eleven days and resulted in her arrest.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baker2012_136-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Baker2012-136">
        [136]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The publicity surrounding the arrest, trial, and appeal sparked birth control activism across the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        [137]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first permanent birth-control clinic was established in Britain in 1921 by
      <a href="/wiki/Marie_Stopes" title="Marie Stopes">
       Marie Stopes
      </a>
      working with the Malthusian League.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        [138]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The clinic, run by midwives and supported by visiting doctors,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
       <a href="#cite_note-139">
        [139]
       </a>
      </sup>
      offered women's birth-control advice and taught them the use of a
      <a href="/wiki/Cervical_cap" title="Cervical cap">
       cervical cap
      </a>
      . Her clinic made contraception acceptable during the 1920s by presenting it in scientific terms. In 1921, Sanger founded the American Birth Control League, which later became the
      <a href="/wiki/Planned_Parenthood" title="Planned Parenthood">
       Planned Parenthood
      </a>
      Federation of America.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_140-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-:1-140">
        [140]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1924 the Society for the Provision of Birth Control Clinics was founded to campaign for municipal clinics; this led to the opening of a second clinic in
      <a href="/wiki/Greengate,_Salford" title="Greengate, Salford">
       Greengate, Salford
      </a>
      in 1926.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
       <a href="#cite_note-141">
        [141]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Throughout the 1920s, Stopes and other
      <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">
       feminist
      </a>
      pioneers, including
      <a href="/wiki/Dora_Russell" title="Dora Russell">
       Dora Russell
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Stella_Browne" title="Stella Browne">
       Stella Browne
      </a>
      , played a major role in breaking down
      <a href="/wiki/Taboo" title="Taboo">
       taboos
      </a>
      about sex. In April 1930 the Birth Control Conference assembled 700 delegates and was successful in bringing birth control and abortion into the political sphere – three months later, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health" title="Ministry of Health">
       Ministry of Health
      </a>
      , in the United Kingdom, allowed local authorities to give birth-control advice in welfare centres.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        [142]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1936 the U.S. court ruled in U.S. v. One Package that medically prescribing contraception to save a persons life or well being was not illegal under the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comstock_Law" title="Comstock Law">
       Comstock Law
      </a>
      ; following this decision, the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Medical_Association" title="American Medical Association">
       American Medical Association
      </a>
      Committee on Contraception revoked its 1936 statement condemning birth control. A national survey in 1937 showed 71 percent of the adult population supported the use of contraception. By 1938 347 birth control clinics were running in the United States despite their advertisement still being illegal.
      <a href="/wiki/First_Lady" title="First Lady">
       First Lady
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">
       Eleanor Roosevelt
      </a>
      publicly supported birth control and family planning.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        [143]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1966,
      <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">
       President Lyndon B. Johnson
      </a>
      started endorsing public funding for family planning services, and the Federal Government began subsidizing birth control services for low-income families.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
       <a href="#cite_note-144">
        [144]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act" title="Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act">
       The Affordable Care Act
      </a>
      , passed into law on March 23, 2010 under President
      <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
       Barack Obama
      </a>
      , requires all plans in the Health Insurance Marketplace to cover contraceptive methods. These include barrier methods, hormonal methods, implanted devices, emergency contraceptives, and sterilization procedures.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
       <a href="#cite_note-145">
        [145]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_methods">
       Modern methods
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Modern methods">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 1909, Richard Richter developed the first intrauterine device made from silkworm gut, which was further developed and marketed in Germany by
      <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Gr%C3%A4fenberg" title="Ernst Gräfenberg">
       Ernst Gräfenberg
      </a>
      in the late 1920s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        [146]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1951, a chemist, named Carl Djerassi from Mexico City made the hormones in progesterone pill using Mexican yams.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        [147]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Djerassi had chemically created the pill but was not equipped to distribute them to patients. Meanwhile,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gregory_Pincus" title="Gregory Pincus">
       Gregory Pincus
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/John_Rock_(American_scientist)" title="John Rock (American scientist)">
       John Rock
      </a>
      with help from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planned_Parenthood_Federation_of_America" title="Planned Parenthood Federation of America">
       Planned Parenthood Federation of America
      </a>
      developed the first birth control pills in the 1950s, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Mestranol/noretynodrel" title="Mestranol/noretynodrel">
       mestranol/noretynodrel
      </a>
      , which became publicly available in the 1960s through the Food and Drug Administration under the name
      <i>
       Enovid
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_140-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-:1-140">
        [140]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
       <a href="#cite_note-148">
        [148]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Medical_abortion" title="Medical abortion">
       Medical abortion
      </a>
      became an alternative to surgical abortion with the availability of
      <a href="/wiki/Prostaglandin_analogue" title="Prostaglandin analogue">
       prostaglandin analogs
      </a>
      in the 1970s and
      <a href="/wiki/Mifepristone" title="Mifepristone">
       mifepristone
      </a>
      in the 1980s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
       <a href="#cite_note-149">
        [149]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">
       Society and culture
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Society and culture">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_positions">
       Legal positions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Legal positions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_reproductive_rights_legislation" title="Timeline of reproductive rights legislation">
       Timeline of reproductive rights legislation
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">
       Human rights
      </a>
      agreements require most governments to provide family planning and contraceptive information and services. These include the requirement to create a national plan for family planning services, remove laws that limit access to family planning, ensure that a wide variety of safe and effective birth control methods are available including emergency contraceptives, make sure there are appropriately trained healthcare providers and facilities at an affordable price, and create a process to review the programs implemented. If governments fail to do the above it may put them in breach of binding international treaty obligations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrintlaw_150-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-hrintlaw-150">
        [150]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In America, Griswold v. Connecticut overturned a state law prohibiting dissemination of contraception information based on a constitutional right to privacy for marital relationships. In 1971, Eisenstadt v. Baird extended this right to privacy to single people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
       <a href="#cite_note-151">
        [151]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2010, the United Nations launched the
      <i>
       Every Woman Every Child
      </i>
      movement to assess the progress toward meeting women's contraceptive needs. The initiative has set a goal of increasing the number of users of modern birth control by 120 million women in the world's 69 poorest countries by the year 2020. Additionally, they aim to eradicate discrimination against girls and young women who seek contraceptives.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gutt2012_152-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gutt2012-152">
        [152]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/American_Congress_of_Obstetricians_and_Gynecologists" title="American Congress of Obstetricians and Gynecologists">
       American Congress of Obstetricians and Gynecologists
      </a>
      (ACOG) recommended in 2014 that oral birth control pills should be
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Over_the_counter_medications" title="Over the counter medications">
       over the counter medications
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
       <a href="#cite_note-153">
        [153]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_views">
       Religious views
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religious views">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Religion_and_birth_control" title="Religion and birth control">
       Religion and birth control
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Religions vary widely in their views of the
      <a href="/wiki/Ethics" title="Ethics">
       ethics
      </a>
      of birth control.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Srikanthan2008_154-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Srikanthan2008-154">
        [154]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
       Roman Catholic Church
      </a>
      officially only accepts
      <a href="/wiki/Natural_family_planning" title="Natural family planning">
       natural family planning
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pope1_155-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pope1-155">
        [155]
       </a>
      </sup>
      although large numbers of Catholics in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_countries" title="Developed countries">
       developed countries
      </a>
      accept and use modern methods of birth control.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
       <a href="#cite_note-156">
        [156]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
       <a href="#cite_note-157">
        [157]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
       <a href="#cite_note-158">
        [158]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Among
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">
       Protestants
      </a>
      there is a wide range of views from
      <a href="/wiki/Quiverfull" title="Quiverfull">
       supporting none
      </a>
      to allowing all methods of birth control.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
       <a href="#cite_note-159">
        [159]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Views in
      <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
       Judaism
      </a>
      range from the stricter
      <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism" title="Orthodox Judaism">
       Orthodox
      </a>
      sect to the more relaxed
      <a href="/wiki/Reform_Judaism" title="Reform Judaism">
       Reform
      </a>
      sect.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jew_BC_160-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-jew_BC-160">
        [160]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">
       Hindus
      </a>
      may use both natural and artificial contraceptives.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu_BC_161-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-hindu_BC-161">
        [161]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A common
      <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
       Buddhist
      </a>
      view is that preventing conception is acceptable, while intervening after conception has occurred is not.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buddhist_BC_162-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-buddhist_BC-162">
        [162]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
       Islam
      </a>
      , contraceptives are allowed if they do not threaten health, although their use is discouraged by some.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        [163]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="World_Contraception_Day">
       World Contraception Day
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: World Contraception Day">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      September 26 is World Contraception Day, devoted to raising awareness and improving education about sexual and reproductive health, with a vision of
      <i>
       a world where every pregnancy is wanted.
      </i>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldContraceptionDay_164-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WorldContraceptionDay-164">
        [164]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is supported by a group of governments and international NGOs, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Population_Affairs" title="Office of Population Affairs">
       Office of Population Affairs
      </a>
      , the Asian Pacific Council on Contraception, Centro Latinamericano Salud y Mujer, the European Society of Contraception and Reproductive Health, the
      <a href="/wiki/German_Foundation_for_World_Population" title="German Foundation for World Population">
       German Foundation for World Population
      </a>
      , the International Federation of Pediatric and Adolescent Gynecology,
      <a href="/wiki/International_Planned_Parenthood_Federation" title="International Planned Parenthood Federation">
       International Planned Parenthood Federation
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Marie_Stopes_International" title="Marie Stopes International">
       Marie Stopes International
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Population_Services_International" title="Population Services International">
       Population Services International
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Population_Council" title="Population Council">
       Population Council
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">
       United States Agency for International Development
      </a>
      (USAID), and
      <a href="/wiki/Women_Deliver" title="Women Deliver">
       Women Deliver
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldContraceptionDay_164-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-WorldContraceptionDay-164">
        [164]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Misconceptions">
       Misconceptions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Misconceptions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      There are a number of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_misconceptions" title="Common misconceptions">
       common misconceptions
      </a>
      regarding sex and pregnancy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
       <a href="#cite_note-165">
        [165]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Douche" title="Douche">
       Douching
      </a>
      after sexual intercourse is not an effective form of birth control.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        [166]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Additionally, it is associated with a number of health problems and thus is not recommended.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
       <a href="#cite_note-167">
        [167]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Women can become pregnant the first time they have sexual intercourse
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        [168]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and in any
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexual_position" title="Sexual position">
       sexual position
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
       <a href="#cite_note-169">
        [169]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is possible, although not very likely, to become pregnant during menstruation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
       <a href="#cite_note-170">
        [170]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Research_directions">
       Research directions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Research directions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Females">
       Females
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Females">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Improvements of existing birth control methods are needed, as around half of those who get pregnant unintentionally are using birth control at the time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Will2012_27-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-Will2012-27">
        [27]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A number of alterations of existing contraceptive methods are being studied, including a better female condom, an improved
      <a href="/wiki/SILCS_diaphragm" title="SILCS diaphragm">
       diaphragm
      </a>
      , a patch containing only progestin, and a vaginal ring containing long-acting progesterone.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jensen2011_171-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jensen2011-171">
        [171]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This vaginal ring appears to be effective for three or four months and is currently available in some areas of the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jensen2011_171-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jensen2011-171">
        [171]
       </a>
      </sup>
      For women who rarely have sex, the taking of the hormonal birth control
      <a href="/wiki/Levonorgestrel" title="Levonorgestrel">
       levonorgestrel
      </a>
      around the time of sex looks promising.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
       <a href="#cite_note-172">
        [172]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A number of methods to perform sterilization via the cervix are being studied. One involves putting
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quinacrine" title="Quinacrine">
       quinacrine
      </a>
      in the uterus which causes scarring and infertility. While the procedure is inexpensive and does not require surgical skills, there are concerns regarding long-term side effects.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cast2010_173-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cast2010-173">
        [173]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another substance,
      <a href="/wiki/Polidocanol" title="Polidocanol">
       polidocanol
      </a>
      , which functions in the same manner is being looked at.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jensen2011_171-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jensen2011-171">
        [171]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A device called
      <a href="/wiki/Essure" title="Essure">
       Essure
      </a>
      , which expands when placed in the fallopian tubes and blocks them, was approved in the United States in 2002.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cast2010_173-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cast2010-173">
        [173]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Males">
       Males
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Males">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Male_contraceptive" title="Male contraceptive">
       Male contraceptive
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Methods of male birth control include condoms, vasectomies and withdrawal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glasier2010_174-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Glasier2010-174">
        [174]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
       <a href="#cite_note-175">
        [175]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Between 25 and 75% of males who are sexually active would use hormonal birth control if it was available for them.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naz2009_120-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Naz2009-120">
        [120]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Glasier2010_174-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Glasier2010-174">
        [174]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A number of hormonal and non-hormonal methods are in trials,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naz2009_120-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Naz2009-120">
        [120]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and there is some research looking at the possibility of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contraceptive_vaccine" title="Contraceptive vaccine">
       contraceptive vaccines
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
       <a href="#cite_note-176">
        [176]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A reversible surgical method under investigation is
      <a href="/wiki/Reversible_inhibition_of_sperm_under_guidance" title="Reversible inhibition of sperm under guidance">
       reversible inhibition of sperm under guidance
      </a>
      (RISUG) which consists of injecting a polymer gel,
      <a href="/wiki/Styrene_maleic_anhydride" title="Styrene maleic anhydride">
       styrene maleic anhydride
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Dimethyl_sulfoxide" title="Dimethyl sulfoxide">
       dimethyl sulfoxide
      </a>
      , into the
      <a href="/wiki/Vas_deferens" title="Vas deferens">
       vas deferens
      </a>
      . An injection with sodium bicarbonate washes out the substance and restores fertility. Another is an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intravas_device" title="Intravas device">
       intravas device
      </a>
      which involves putting a
      <a href="/wiki/Polyurethane" title="Polyurethane">
       urethane
      </a>
      plug into the
      <a href="/wiki/Vas_deferens" title="Vas deferens">
       vas deferens
      </a>
      to block it. A combination of an
      <a href="/wiki/Androgen" title="Androgen">
       androgen
      </a>
      and a
      <a href="/wiki/Progestin" title="Progestin">
       progestin
      </a>
      seems promising, as do
      <a href="/wiki/Selective_androgen_receptor_modulator" title="Selective androgen receptor modulator">
       selective androgen receptor modulators
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Naz2009_120-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Naz2009-120">
        [120]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Ultrasound" title="Ultrasound">
       Ultrasound
      </a>
      and methods to heat the testicles have undergone preliminary studies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
       <a href="#cite_note-177">
        [177]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_animals">
       Other animals
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Birth_control&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Other animals">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Neutering" title="Neutering">
       Neutering
      </a>
      or spaying, which involves removing some of the reproductive organs, is often carried out as a method of birth control in household pets. Many
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_shelters" title="Animal shelters">
       animal shelters
      </a>
      require these procedures as part of adoption agreements.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
       <a href="#cite_note-178">
        [178]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In large animals the surgery is known as
      <a href="/wiki/Castration" title="Castration">
       castration
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
       <a href="#cite_note-179">
        [179]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Birth control is also being considered as an alternative to hunting as a means of controlling
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overpopulation_in_wild_animals" title="Overpopulation in wild animals">
       overpopulation in wild animals
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boyle_2009_180-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Boyle_2009-180">
        [180]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contraceptive_vaccine" title="Contraceptive vaccine">
       Contraceptive vaccines
      </a>
      have been found to be effective in a number of different animal populations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
       <a href="#cite_note-181">
        [181]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
       <a href="#cite_note-182">
        [182]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kenyan goat herders fix a skirt, called and
      <a href="/wiki/Olor" title="Olor">
       olor
      </a>
      , to male goats to prevent them from impregnating female goats.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
       <a href="#cite_note-183">
        [183]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
